Spring and Autumn Fishing Boat

Guiding Public Opinion 194

— 19

Since the beginning of history, it can be said that public opinion in our country has never been on the right track. The scholars and commoners always speak without restraint and like to talk nonsense. How great is the power of the emperor! It seems that everyone should sing his praises. During the reign of Emperor Yao, the world was at peace, and nothing happened. An old man named Huai Rang-fu, over eighty years old, sang a song on the road. Onlookers said, "How great is the virtue of the Emperor!" Rang-fu said, "I work when the sun rises and rest when the sun sets. I dig a well to drink from and till the field for food. What virtue does the Emperor have for me!" This is the Rang Fu Song, which is passed down in later generations and is recorded in Emperor Wang Century. Just imagine, during the reign of Emperor Yao, the world was already in "great harmony" and the people were "free from incident," but Rang-fu was still dissatisfied and said, "What virtue does the Emperor have for me?" This seems to be slandering Emperor Yao. Fortunately, Emperor Yao was benevolent and wise and had a forgiving heart. Otherwise, wouldn't Rang-fu be in danger! This is one story of public opinion not being on the right track.

During the reign of King Li of Zhou, public opinion was rampant. The more he listened, the more annoyed he became, so he wanted to "prevent the people's mouths" to "stop slander." However, the result was also equal to zero. This is because he did not know how to guide public opinion.

Also, during the reign of Emperor Qin Shihuang, those who engaged in gossip were executed. Although the criminal law was undeniably strict to the extreme, he did not know how to guide public opinion, so it was no different from bailing water to stop boiling, and the country was eventually destroyed as a result.

Coming down to the late Qing Dynasty, the Qing court established the nine-year preparatory constitutionalism. The most brilliant sentence in the imperial edict was "All political affairs should be made public to public opinion." This cannot but be said to be "great imperial words." However, because no methods for guidance were established, the constitutionalism had not yet been prepared, and the Qing Dynasty was already delivered into the hands of "public opinion"!

A few examples are enough to prove that it is necessary to guide public opinion. As for how to guide it, I am ashamed to be a fool and have no precedent to follow, so I cannot contribute my humble opinion. The Book of Songs says, "Without knowledge, without understanding, follow the rules of the Emperor." This was a saying used to guide the scholars and commoners of the time, and public opinion can of course be included. However, times have changed, and this principle is no longer applicable. I do not know if foreign countries have good ways to guide public opinion because I have not been abroad. In short, this matter is of great importance, and proper regulations should be drafted. If they are made into established laws, then we must rely on virtuous people.

By the Huangpu River 195

— Huang Kewei

The Huangpu River, with its tender yellow water, screams hysterically. Beast-like warships, eyes wide with fury, glare. Massive cannons open their shining steel mouths, leering at the statue of peace on the riverbank.

The dredging machine trails its long iron pigtails, baring its steel-knife-like fangs, swallowing the mud and spewing it into the boat as if suffering from cholera.

On the docks, suffocating smoke billows, like black plum blossoms of coal ash. It flies onto the bodies of the coolies. Heavy wooden crates press down on their shoulders, their arms twitching with rat-like muscle contractions. Step by agonizing step, they climb the thread-like gangplank. Crystalline beads of sweat race down their backs. "Hang yo, hang yo," their cries sound like wounded wolves howling wildly in the silent midnight, painful tears welling in their eyes. Meanwhile, the gold-domed Sassoon House raises its head and laughs at them.

Merchant ships sailing from beyond the Wusong estuary float alongside the docks, spewing white foam. Though many coolies unload the heavy burdens from their bellies, black fumes still puff from their long mouths, as if trying to alleviate the fatigue of their long journeys.

The saltwater girl smokes, blowing round, mesmerizing smoke rings like a fish blowing bubbles. Her enchanting pupils glance sidelong at a group of white sailors, who swarm around like flies to rotten meat.

Under the street trees that spread like green gauze umbrellas, Chinese nannies stroll with Pekingese dogs. Several foreign children, with toy wooden guns slung on their backs, happily eat toffee and jump around. Jiangbei children, searching for seashells, look at their bright silk clothes, and a sense of sorrow invades their pure hearts. They smile bitterly, wipe the mud from their legs with their blue cloth gowns, and walk towards the Sixteen Pups area.

Casual Talk on Cartoons 196

— Qian Yun (author), Wen Dongliang (artist)

Only Seeking Room and Board, Not Caring About Salary

In Shanghai, earning fifty yuan a month is considered “eating well.” Unfortunately, buying a shirt and trousers for the wife, some pastries for the children, cannot be considered wasteful. Plus, one's own beard stubble needs shaving. Saving money in the bank is simply an empty dream. Every day feels like being so pressured by life that one can't even stretch a little. But do you think this is okay?

Especially since Shanghai is like a big rice bucket, people from all over rush here to find food. Out of ten thousand people, if one or two manage to hold a rice bowl, they are already considered lucky. Certainly, these lucky ones can no longer worry about the taste of the rice.

Professions are being squeezed out! Those who come are still like a tide. Needless to say, things are getting worse and worse. So, more and more people are only seeking room and board, not caring about salary. In other words, they only care about filling their own stomachs. They can't take care of their wives, children, and elders, so whatever they can grab, they grab!

This kind of phenomenon in society is, of course, terrifying. But...

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 197

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 10: Hearing His Words, Her Heart Fluttered; His Wish to Be Ennobled Seemed Distant; Seeing His Leisure, She Admired His Dedication to the Country

Seeing the girl looking so dejected, Madam Jiang was puzzled. She thought that Guizhi had been subjected to some unkind words when she went to the Liu's to ask for the pills. Lying on the kang, she gently asked Guizhi: "My illness is not serious, why did I tell you to go ask for pills? If someone offends you, you’ll pout." Guizhi said: "Who offended me? Madam Liu didn't say a second word. As soon as she heard we wanted pills, she immediately agreed to get them." Madam Jiang said: "Since they didn't offend you, why are you angry?" Guizhi just lowered her head and sewed, answering casually: "I'm just feeling annoyed." Madam Jiang said: "Whether one is happy or annoyed, there's always a reason. Listening to you, it seems like you're getting annoyed for no reason at all." Guizhi said: "Of course there's a reason." Madam Jiang said: "What is it?" Guizhi said: "Don't ask me. If you ask, and I tell you, I'll be even more annoyed." Hearing this, Madam Jiang thought, "Something is strange about this. She was happy when she left, so why is she pouting now? And she said Madam Liu didn't offend her, so what is it?" As Madam Jiang thought this, her eyes kept watching Guizhi's face. But after two days, Guizhi was still like this, and Madam Jiang began to understand that it must be the Zhao family marriage that she was unhappy with. She must have heard some words outside that day that stirred up her worries, so she just kept getting angry. This is a free era. Since the girl doesn't want this marriage, saying anything is useless. Not only will it not succeed, but even if it does succeed, the elders will suffer because of it. So why bother? Therefore, Madam Jiang suddenly understood and stopped mentioning the matter, and after half a month, the once-lively Yang-Zhao marriage faded away. (117)

A Study of Walking Posture 198

— Bai He

"Everyone can walk, but everyone walks differently." According to a "Walking Posture" PhD, the most appropriate posture is the "eight-character walk." The method of the "eight-character walk" is to align the left heel with the midpoint of the right foot, and the extension line of the left foot perpendicularly reaches the midpoint of the right foot. The tip of the left shoe, the tip of the right shoe, and the heel form an "isosceles triangle." Taking a step forward, the tip of the right shoe and the tip and heel of the left shoe also form an "isosceles triangle." It is said that with this posture, the center of gravity is in the "chest," so it can expand the chest.

The opposite of this method is called the "reverse eight-character walk." The "eight-character walk" is writing the character "eight" upside down, starting with the heel. The "reverse eight-character walk" is the opposite of the "eight-character walk." Although geometrically, it also forms an "isosceles triangle," this "eight" is written starting with the tip of the shoe. Walking with this posture, the center of gravity is also opposite of the "eight-character walk." The focus is on the "back," so most old gentlemen with a waddling gait walk with a "reverse eight-character walk."

The "one-character walk" is also a type of walking posture. The so-called "one-character walk" is maintaining the "parallel line" relationship between the extension lines of the left and right feet. When standing still, the two feet look like the character "one." The only wonderful use of this posture is that the "center of gravity" is in the "abdomen," which can form a "big belly." "High-class Chinese" and "tycoons" are most skilled at the "one-character walk."

The movement of the two feet in the "vertical one-character walk" is completely different from the "one-character walk." The "vertical one-character walk" is aligning the left heel with the right toe. Taking a step forward, aligning the right heel with the left toe. The two feet are connected to form the Arabic numeral "1." Walking with this posture can develop the "buttocks" into extremely high curves, making them plump and abundant. This is because the center of gravity of this posture is not too high or too low, but right at the buttocks. To be a "modern girl" with "rich sensuality," one must walk with the "vertical one-character walk."

These are the four major principles of "walking posture." Although they change endlessly and can be produced continuously, they are never outside of these few principles. If readers don't think it's meaningless, pay attention and study them, and perhaps it will be strangely interesting.

Children's Paradise

Little Dog Dinggan 199

— Yin Feng

"What wonderful weather today!" Little Dog Dinggan thought. "I want to go to the farm and play, and see if there's anything fun or interesting."

After thinking for a while, he ran and walked into the farm, scaring the hens to scatter in all directions, dodging left and right. He ran straight to the side of the chicken coop, where several diligent hens were busy laying eggs.

"Now I see something interesting," Dinggan said.

Just as he walked into the chicken coop, an older hen said, "Dinggan, what are you doing here? We're busy laying eggs. Please go out quickly!"

"I won't go out!" Dinggan said angrily and scoldingly. "Before I leave, you must teach me how to lay eggs."

"Okay, I'll teach you," a fat, brown hen said. "Watch closely." Then she climbed into her nest! Cluck! Cluck! Cluck cluck cluck, she called for a while, and then a brown egg, just like herself, was laid.

"That's easy," the little dog said. "Let me try." So he climbed into the nest, squatting very comfortably. The old hen watched him from the side. Dinggan used all his wits and skills, trying to imitate the old hen's call, but the result was pitiful.

"It doesn't take that long," the old hen said, feeling that her nest wasn't very comfortable herself, and perhaps Dinggan thought it was very comfortable.

"I can't lay an egg," Dinggan said disappointedly, "but I really want to take a nap here."

"But I don't think you can," the old hen said.

"But look," Dinggan said, "I will, I'm going to do it right now."

"Then I'll peck you," the old hen said.

"Pah! I'm not afraid of your pecking," Dinggan said, "you can't hurt me."

"Oh, then you just watch me," the old hen said, using all her strength and pecking Dinggan hard.

"Woof! Woof! Woof!" Dinggan was hurt by the old hen's peck and barked loudly, immediately running away, out of the chicken coop, and running non-stop until he reached his home.

Star Money 200

— Yin Feng

Once upon a time, there was a girl whose parents had died. She was truly lonely and miserable. She was so poor that she didn't even have a house, and so miserable that she didn't even have a bed. Besides the clothes she was wearing and a small piece of bread given to her by someone, she had nothing else. She had no place to live and no place to sleep, and was truly suffering unspeakably.

However, she was a very kind-hearted and devout person. Having no place to live, she walked alone in a certain direction, thinking that she could reach a paradise and a happy country. Unexpectedly, she met a suffering person on the road. He said,

"My head is extremely cold. Please give me something to cover it." Therefore, she took off her headscarf and gave it to him. As she walked a short distance further, she met a child who didn't even have a short coat to wear and was so cold that he was about to freeze to death. So she took off her short coat and gave it to him. As she walked further, someone asked her for a coat, and she also gave him one. "It's night now, and no one will see me. It's okay to take off my shirt and give it to him." She took off her shirt and gave it to the child. At this time, she had nothing left on her head, body, or in her hands. She was just standing there when suddenly several stars fell from the sky. She wasn't scared, but just watched blankly, and saw that when the stars landed on the ground, they all turned into flat, hard, bright, and shiny pieces of gold coins. Although she had just given her shirt to the child, now she found a brand new, exquisite shirt in front of her. So she gathered the gold coins on the ground, wrapped them in the shirt, and from then on, she enjoyed a lifetime of wealth and happiness.

Free Talk

On the Merits and Demerits of Huaide and Bao粹 201

— Ru Niu

Mr. Hitler does not allow any other parties within Germany, and even the subdued National Power Party can hardly survive. This seems to have quite moved some of our heroes, who are already praising his "drastic measures." But in reality, this is just one side of him and his ilk. On the other side, they are also very meticulous. There is a song to prove it:

The flea has become a high official,

Leading a gang everywhere.

The empress and concubines are all afraid,

No one dares to touch it.

Even if it bites and itches,

How can you possibly squash it?

Ai haha, ai haha, haha, ai haha!

This is a well-known world-famous song, "The Flea Song," but it has been banned in Germany. Of course, this is definitely not out of respect for fleas, but because it satirizes high officials. But it's also not because the satire is "the ramblings of old men from the previous century," but because the song is "un-German." The great and small heroes of Huaide inevitably have some areas where they are out of touch.

China is also a place that gives birth to meticulous figures, sometimes able to think very carefully. For example, this year, the Beijing Social Affairs Bureau petitioned the Municipal Government to ban women from raising male dogs, writing:

"...After investigation, the association of female humans and male dogs is not only harmful to health, but also more likely to cause shameless and obscene scandals. According to our country, a land of propriety and righteousness, this is also not allowed by custom. We hereby issue a strict ban. Except for guard dogs and hunting dogs, any male dogs kept by women will be executed without mercy, as a means of prohibition."

The standpoint of both countries is based on "national essence," but China's spirit is more grand, because Germany only prohibits everyone from singing that song, while China will not only make it difficult for "female humans" to keep dogs, but even "male dogs" will be beheaded. This has a great impact on Pekingese dogs. Driven by the instinct to preserve themselves and the need to adapt to the times, they will inevitably transform into "guard dog hunting dog" models.

The Heart of a Man 202

— Shi Heng

"A hero does not shed tears lightly, only because he has not reached the point of heartbreak." This is a line sung by the hero Lin Chong in the famous Chinese opera "Night Flight." When I heard this line, I engraved it in my memory. I felt that it was the highest expression of the male heart.

So I also wanted to forge my heart like a piece of iron, enduring all the so-called suffering in the world. With tears swirling in my eyes, I would swallow them back into my stomach. I was very proud of my strength, and I scorned all feminine people.

But God would torment me. He made me fall in love with a person, a woman with the most delicate heart. Her emotions were so winding, her nerves were so sharp, while I was an emotionally barren child, crude and even more honest. We lived together, unable to understand each other. I scorned her, and she doubted me. Finally, one night, she cried, a heart-wrenching cry! And then, the next day, she quietly left, without any nostalgia.

The demon was still riding on me. I thought, should a man diminish himself for the love of a woman? I grinned and drank to celebrate the woman's escape. I even thanked God for giving me freedom again.

But one can never deceive oneself for long. In the depths of the night, the heart opened its eyes and softly whispered, "You love her. You can't live without her, you know?"

Gradually, a slight pain came from the heart. I struggled to resist it, not letting it overcome me. I, a person with the strongest male heart! I laughed maniacally, stopping the tears in my eyes, but what kind of laughter was it?

Have you ever wandered among desolate tombs in the deep night and heard the laughter of ghosts? That is the kind of terrible sound!

Next, I felt that if my emotions didn't give me some relief, I would become a spirit. Why shouldn't I cry out loud, using tears to moisten my pain, to show my repentance, and to lower my head before God and before humanity?

The strong, powerful, and huge hand that had always been pushing me from behind now showed its power even more, and I was completely overcome by it.

I lay on my pillow and cried loudly. Those tears, those precious tears! At the same time, I remembered Goethe's famous line:

"He who has never eaten his bread with tears,

Who has never spent sleepless nights

Weeping and waiting for the dawn,

He does not know you, you great powers!"

The Foolish Bridegroom 203

— Ye Rong

Several people were enjoying the cool breeze on the bridgehead. As I walked onto the bridge, they all squeezed their eyes and stopped talking. Xiao Lin asked me, "Fu Gen, is your wedding day soon?"

I nodded and walked past, hearing them burst into laughter behind me. The laughter was like a fire, scorching my back.

What's so funny? Just because a person is born a little poor, does that mean he shouldn't have a wedding day and marry a wife? Everyone says I'm foolish, but it's just that I was born a little poor. Where am I foolish? I'm twenty-three years old this year. Normally, people my age would have been married and had children long ago. But me, the girls far and near all like me but are unwilling to marry me. Isn't that because I'm poor? My dad was so angry that I couldn't get married that he said he would buy land as dowry to win back this honor, even if the whole family went hungry afterward. Now the marriage is finally settled. Although the girl lives far away, I heard that she is very young and her family is well-off. My dad is happy, and I'm happy too. Even the gifts and jewelry have already cost more than a thousand dollars. The matchmakers are Elder Xiang Sheng and Mr. You Sheng.

So I turned around and spat at them. They were gesturing and talking happily. Seeing me turn around, Xiao Lin raised his hand and shouted loudly, "Fu Gen, your wife won't be coming through the door today. The wedding won't happen."

The wedding won't happen? What a load of crap. If she hasn't come in two days, it's because the road is so far, and two days is naturally not enough to get here. But she must come today. Wasn't my dad just telling me to urge Elder Xiang Sheng to talk with him about it? I believe the bride will definitely come.

Elder Xiang Sheng wasn't home. When I turned back, the people on the bridge had all scattered. The sky had already turned dark. Dad heard that he wasn't home and sent someone to invite Mr. You Sheng, but he wasn't home either. Someone said that there must have been a change of plans and the matchmakers were hiding. Everyone was helpless and the guests all sighed and dispersed. Could it be that something had really changed with the wedding? I couldn't figure out the mystery, but seeing my dad's face, it seemed very difficult.

This was the third day. When I got up in the morning, everyone seemed to have forgotten about the events of the previous two days, and the guests became lively again as usual. I had been worried all night, and I was finally able to settle down a bit. Dad sent someone to the girl's home in Qibao Bridge early in the morning to urge them to come. Xiao Lin's words couldn't be accurate. After the wedding day is over, I'll spit in his face. ...

...However, however, it was getting late again. The guests in the hall were all wiping their sweat and talking about it. But the bride still didn't appear. Dad sighed and said, "We've been tricked."

What trick? Could it be that the wedding won't happen again this time? I couldn't believe it. I thought it was Xiao Lin who was causing trouble in the middle, otherwise how would he have known in advance that my wedding wouldn't happen?

So I wanted to go find him and settle the score. I went to his house. He was already gone, he had run away. I went to the bridge, and a group of people were gathered there. I saw Xiao Lin in the middle. He couldn't dodge in time and was grabbed by me. He hadn't expected that I would find him here.

Unexpectedly, I slapped him twice in the face first. He turned his head and shouted, "What are you doing?"

I said, "What trick did you play to prevent me from having a wedding?" Everyone around me burst out laughing. Xiao Lin struggled in my hands, trying to escape, but I held him tightly. They had agreed not to help each other. Hands reached out from all sides, and then they snatched Xiao Lin away from my hands. I fell to the ground myself. They laughed as they held me to the ground. Someone said, "Come and see the foolish bridegroom! We'll give him a wedding today."

I fainted in their hands. When I woke up, there was only me left on the bridge, and frogs were croaking all around, just like their laughter. I decided to jump into the water, but then I thought, maybe the bride has already entered the door? So I stood up and walked down the bridge.

I thought the bride wouldn't not come. The road is so far, and three days is naturally not enough to get here.

The Finale of the Gongs and Drums 204

— He Ru

Having already written the article "Revisiting the Gongs and Drums," I recently heard that Mr. Luo Fu has already written a rebuttal, but it has not yet been published (Editor's note: i.e., Mr. Luo Fu's article from yesterday). I don't know what he will say. I expect he has some new and wonderful interpretations. There is no doubt about that. But I am ashamed of my meager knowledge and have no literary baggage to display. Still, I dare to write this third article, one to somewhat exhaust the meaning of my previous articles, and the other to hope to obtain the high opinion of an expert in music. A scholar discussing opera is a presumptuous illusion. The actual situation on the stage, I dare to question and truly appreciate.

However, I have a few things to clarify. One is that I fear readers will be dazzled by the confusion, and the other is that I want to prevent the debater from digressing from the main point. Therefore, in my previous two articles, I did not hesitate to reiterate the key points. First, "Speaking of Kunqu Opera, has it ever not valued gongs and drums?" I cited the words of Li Liweng and Tong Fumin as proof. I am merely quoting old sayings, not offering new interpretations. If there are any errors, I will not take responsibility. Second, I speculate on the historical origins of gongs and drums and martial arts in our old operas, believing that they came from wrestling matches and dance dramas with masks from the Qin, Han, Sui, and Tang dynasties. Thus, I say that China has had drama as a concept since its origin. Gongs and drums have been inseparable from it. I am only saying that there are gongs and drums, not that the types and ways of playing the gongs and drums are the same as they are today. Third, I say that the words in Gu's "Casual Talks from the Guest Seat," referring to the large four-part suites of northern opera, inserting miscellaneous skills such as "cuo dian quan," "dancing Guanyin," "hundred-foot banner," or "jumping duizi" as martial arts, are clearly remnants of miscellaneous skills in acrobatics. However, I have only read dozens of kinds of Yuan dramas from northern opera. I am completely ignorant of the actual situation on the stage. I can only comment on this and dare not pretend to be an expert.

What I want to add now is that Mr. Luo Fu said, "Around the Wanli period of the Ming dynasty, neither northern opera nor southern opera used gongs and drums at all," and also said, "Southern opera initially did not use gongs and drums." He said that because I cited Li Liweng's words on gongs and drums as proof, and then said that "Liweng's theory was published when Kunqu Opera was declining," this was the biggest loophole in my argument. I have already refuted this in my repeated arguments. Wei Liangfu's "Music Laws" says: "Singing without accompaniment is called 'cold bench.' It is not like the momentum of gongs and drums on the stage. It requires elegance, solemnity, freshness, and gentleness." Wei was the founder of Kunqu Opera, and his theories on music already included gongs and drums. How can you strongly claim that "around the Wanli period of the Ming dynasty, neither northern opera nor southern opera used gongs and drums at all?" Only Mr. Luo Fu has this bold new interpretation. And he boasts that it is correct. Furthermore, Zhu Zhuzhai's "Poetry Talks from the Quiet Dwelling" says that when Kang Dui Shan died, his family had nothing of value except three hundred pairs of waist drums. Lu Kanru's "Poetry History" says that there were three hundred pairs of large and small drums. According to research, Kang Hai was a person from the Chenghua and Jiajing periods, about the same time as Wei Liangfu, or slightly earlier. He was a famous northern opera author at the time. It has not been heard that he also worked on southern opera. What was he storing drums for? The number is especially alarming. But I dare not rush to offer a new interpretation, saying that it is proof that northern opera had gongs and drums.

This is the extent of my argument, and this is the extent of my response. In political disputes, one often views the gains and losses like chickens and insects. To use writing as weapons again, how can I still have a thatched heart!

Radish Whiskers 205

— Written by Jules Renard, Translated by Lin Qu

Radish Whiskers' Photo Album (Continued)

Twenty

"Radish Whiskers, won't you give me a quiet, ladylike smile?" said the Le Picque wife.

"When someone cries, they should know why they are crying," she said.

She also said;

"What do you want me to do? When he is slapped, he doesn't even shed a tear."

Twenty-one

She also said;

"If there is a stain in the sky, a pile of animal dung on the bed, it is all prepared for him."

"Whatever he happens to think of, it's always unfinished."

"He is so proud that he is willing to kill himself to get attention."

Twenty-two

Indeed, Radish Whiskers wanted to kill himself in a bucket of clear water. He bravely submerged his nose and mouth in the water, but just then, a clergyman passed by, overturned the bucket, splashed water on his feet, and saved Radish Whiskers' life.

Twenty-three

Sometimes, when the Le Picque wife mentioned Radish Whiskers, she said;

"He is as incapable of cunning as I am. Rather than saying he is evil, I would say he is stupid. His mind is too dull to come up with any tricks."

Sometimes she would admit that if he wasn't eaten by piglets, he would develop in the future.

Twenty-four

"If someone would give me a wooden horse as a gift, like they gave to my older brother Felix," Radish Whiskers thought, "then I would jump on it and ride away at full speed."

American Cotton Rises Due to Acreage Reduction Campaign 213

New York, June 30th, reports on the cotton market for the week: At the beginning of the week, news of the cotton field reduction campaign spread, coupled with strong wheat market, stable cotton cloth, and general industrial activity picking up, there were cries of poor cotton crops in the Southwest cotton belt. Speculators bought in droves, and cotton prices rose sharply. Profit-taking followed, and sales in the South also increased. The fluctuating rise and fall of foreign exchange, the contradictory news of currency stability in various countries, and its final impact on the expansion plan in the United States, later caused confusion in the cotton cloth market. Regarding the reduction of cotton fields, the initial news was extremely optimistic. Some farmers, in view of the sharp rise in prices, gradually expressed their unwillingness to remove their cotton, which was still growing. However, the official market issued a warning that if the acreage reduction plan fails, the existing relatively high prices will not last long. The weather bureau reported that the new cotton crop can withstand unharmed under dry weather conditions. The government report estimating cotton fields on July 8 will not take into account any reductions.

Business Economics Twenty

Thoughts on Identifying the Authenticity of Tung Oil 224

Since white tung oil began to be sold to Europe and the United States, it has been four or five years ago, when exports were at their peak, and prices soared to more than forty taels per dan. Because the price is high and the profit is thick, there are endless ways to fake it. At first, the heart of the cypress was mixed in (that is, the kernel inside the cypress seed). Because it has the effect of regulating both sexes, it is still relatively decent. After that, things got worse and worse. Almost all oils that were cheaper than white tung oil were mixed in, and even mineral yellow oil (spindle oil) was the main ingredient for faking it. Only a few reputable firms are not willing to be completely bad. For those who only seek profit, the goods they sell are only 20% to 30% genuine tung oil. As for identifying the authenticity, it is absolutely not easy, so foreign firms must use specific gravity equipment to test the degree. Roughly speaking, among vegetable oils, tung oil has the highest degree. Genuine original tung oil has a degree between 1.5170. Therefore, what foreign firms handle is at least 1.5168. If it does not reach this degree, the goods will be returned. For this reason, the goods for export cannot be faked and are still original. What is sold domestically is completely unbearable. Those who are deceived are the users, who may be greedy for a little cheapness and suffer a great loss. If you want to identify the authenticity with your eyes, it is really not easy. The usual way to look is to first observe its color, which is light and tender yellow, and there is no kerosene gloss on the surface. Then smell its odor, which is purely the odor of tung oil and has no other odors. The texture is heavy, and at temperatures below fifty degrees, it freezes like yellow wax. Moreover, tung oil is heavy, while yellow oil is a mineral product and is light. Heavy things sink, and light things float. If you observe carefully, it is not difficult to understand. If you have this vision, you will not be deceived.

Hongjiang tung oil is made from white tung oil, so it has no way to be exported. White tung oil can still be faked, and Hongjiang tung oil must be faked even more severely. There is a distinction between genuine and counterfeit brands. The quality of the goods is only distinguished by the brand names of various oil presses. Although each has a registered trademark, they are not taken seriously. The so-called "certain brand" and "certain brand" on the market are all the brand names of the oil presses. Its origin is far away in Hongjiang Town, southern Hunan, and most of its sales are in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Therefore, counterfeiting and other things are also in the Suzhou and Hangzhou areas. Because Hongjiang tung oil has no degree to test after being transformed, it is even more difficult to identify. It all relies on the three aspects of color, smell, and taste to judge the authenticity, which is very difficult. Some use the residue from the oil press and mix it in, and some refine the yellow oil and remove its odor, so that it is not distinguished by insiders. Users can only look at its color, bright light, and pure smell. However, if buyers recognize the brand name, there are counterfeit brands, so you must observe the authenticity of the trademark. However, there are also cases where the bucket is a real bucket and the oil is fake oil. It can be said that there is nothing that cannot be done, and it is impossible to distinguish everything. You can only ask for a more reputable store.

Home
